Crime stats convey 
inaccurate image
The World According to CMU 
Crime Statistics

5
Letters to the Editor
; By law, campus crime statis
tics must be released to the pub
lic. However, the current method 
off determining such statistics is 
misleading, which in turn mis
informs the public about the 
slafety of this campus.
; The official CMU statistics for 
the period from 1990-1992, 
available on pages 8 and 9 of 
this weeks Tartan, dont reflect 
the number of all reported 
crimes, but rather cite the num
ber of crimes that are consid
ered founded by the police. An 
unfounded crime report is one 
tpat is considered by the police 
tb have little or no credibility, or 
E^ny report that does not result 
ih charges being brought.
| Furthermore, only crimes that 
olccur on property within the 
jurisdiction of Campus Police 
s(re included. The statistics 
wouldnt show the assault of a 
CMU student on Walnut Street 
ih Shadyside, because that area 
ipnt under the jurisdiction of 
the University.
; Rapes, for example, are only 
included in the crime statistics 
when they are reported to Cam
pus Police. Thus, a rape reported 
to Housing, Student Affairs, or 
the Counseling Center will not 
be included in the statistics un
less charges are filed. This ex
plains why the report shows that 
r|o rapes have occurred in the 
past three years. Also, if a rape 
i? reported to Campus Police, 
but is unfounded, it is not re
corded.
!The student body may not
1 Its nice to know that organi
zations such as the Student Dor
mitory Council (SDC) are work
ing to promote wider perspec
tives and views through pro
grams such as the annual Sex 
Week, which occurred for the 
third time at CMU this past 
Week.
[Topics like premarital sex are 
controversial, and when dis
cussed at a place like CMU, 
niany different opinions are go
ing to be presented, both on the 
importance of abstinence and, 
for those who choose not to wait, 
s^ife, and responsible sex.
Sometimes its hard to repre
sent both views, but SDC, al
though it formerly had spon
sored all of the events of Sex 
Week, has extended it to in
clude many campus organizatipns so that different voices may 
be heard. This way, people with 
all views on sex and sexuality 
cdn participate.
InterVarsity Christian Fellow
ship, for example was allowed 
to join in the events by sharing 
their views on abstinence 
through such programs as Why 
Waiting is Worth the Wait.
The ideas behind Sex Week, 
promoting safety, knowledge, 
aiid awareness, are well-appre
ciated and needed. The variety 
of programs available allowed 
tlie input of a number of view
points, such as that presented 
in Sexually Transmitted Dis
eases: It Can Happen toYou.It 
is: important to remember the
know it is being misled. The 
Security statistics indicate that 
they are in compliance with 
Pennsylvania Legislative Act 
73, section 3. The report indi
cates where to find more infor
mation. This is unacceptable. 
The exact method of determin
ing the statistics should be made 
known to those who read the 
statistics and those whom they 
affect.
The Security report should be 
expanded. Crimes that occur to 
students off-campus should be 
noted, perhaps under a second 
category. The report should also 
include statistics of crimes re
ported to Student Affairs, Hous
ing, and the Counseling Center 
as well, since some students may 
be unwilling to report crimes to 
the police.
The University is following the 
letter of the law. However, it is 
negligent by not following the 
laws intent. The law was in
tended to inform the public of 
the safety of college campuses. 
In an urban campus like 
Carnegie Mellon, those statis
tics should include crimes that 
occur to students off campus as 
well as the number of crimes 
reported to administrative en
tities other than the Campus 
Police.
Students and parents need to 
know how safe this area is. The 
administration does not aid stu
dent or parents by following only 
the letter of the law and misrep
resenting the number of crimes 
on campus.
dangers of sex while presenting 
events that state the facts on 
how to keep yourself as safe as 
possible.
We do, however, encourage the 
involvement of more student 
groups, especially those that 
hold certain particular views 
with regard to sexual activity. 
SDC should definitely seek the 
involvement of many organiza
tions for next years Sex Week. 
Likewise, other groups should 
come to SDC if they have ideas 
for an event and make it a point 
to participate in Sex Week and 
share in the learning. This in
volvement will truly serve to 
enhance the effect of Sex Week.
Of the many on-campus orga
nizations, only seven besides 
SDC sponsored a program dur
ing the week.
Surely more groups than that 
have something to say about 
these issues. A program like 
Sex Week seems like the perfect 
opportunity for student groups 
like cmuOUT to be heard.
Finally, congratulations to 
SDC for working so hard this 
past week and for consciously 
trying to make Sex Week more 
balanced and reflective of our 
diverse CMU community.
Also, kudos to SDC and AB 
Lectures for getting Dr. Ruth to 
speak tonight at 8 pm in Sldbo 
Ballroom. This lecture, and all 
the events of Sex Week were a 
service to the campus and com
munity that did not go unno
ticed or unappreciated.
Campus Police lacks 
concern for student safety

Carnegie Mellon sheds some light on campus security
Theres no reason to be in the dark about campus security. A team of Carnegie Mellon police officers, security guards, and housing and student affairs staff members 
work to keep students, faculty, staff and visitors informed and safe on the campus and adjacent areas. These professionals are concerned with the safety and welfare 
of the campus community and are best able to answer questions about campus security.
Campus Security Staff
How many police officers are on campus?
Twenly-one armed officers constitute the police stall. They are empowered to make 
an arrest on Carnegie Mellon properly or any areas adjacent to the university. 
Additionally, there are 22 security guards, live radio dispatchers and two traffic 
monitors on the slaff. Fool patrols by guaids support the officers' surveillance ol 
the campus academic buildings and residence halls.
What can the officers do in an emergency?
Ollicers. Including three sergeanls, a lieutenant and Ihe director ol security, are 
sworn and commissioned under Ihe General Laws ol the Commonwealth ol 
Pennsylvania. They are certified under Act 235 prior lo duly and receive firearms 
and Emergency Medical Training. Officers also receive specialized training in 
currenl concerns, such as aulo thell, drug awareness, crime search procedure and 
hazardous materials. Sworn ollicers receive their authority from Act 501 ol Ihe 
Pennsylvania Consolidated Statutes. The Act reads: "Such policemen, so 
appointed, shall severally possess and exercise all Ihe powers ol a police officer in 
this Commonwealth. In and upon, and in Ihe immediate and adjacent vicinity ol, 
Ihe properly ol Ihe corporation." Ollicers are also trained under Act 120  
Municipal Police Training and Education Acl.
What authority do security guards have?
While they are not sworn ollicers. each guard receives orientation training in areas 
such as building security, key control, procedures related to arrests by ollicers, 
and criminal and palrol procedures; Guards also train in specialty areas Including 
medical emergencies and hazardous wasles. They assist the campus police In all 
ol these areas.
How do the security guards supplement campus police patrols?
The guards regularly palrol academic buildings and residence halls every night ol 
Ihe year During the day. two traffic monitors also patrol campus parking areas.
A Safe City and Campus
What about crime in Pittsburgh?
Pittsburgh's relalivety low incidence ol crime, along with its educational, cultural, 
sporls and geographic benefits, helped lo secure its slatus as Ihe most livable city 
in America The Cily ol Pittsburgh and Allegheny Counly Police Forces, as well as 
Ihe Pennsylvania Stale Police and the FBI, are Ihe major elements in a crimeprevention network that Includes the campus police departments of all Pittsburgh 
colleges and universities. Students allending Carnegie Mellon benelit from Ihe 
cooperative relationship Campus Police enjoys with federal, slate, county and cily 
police agencies.
What does this cooperation involve?
The university's Department ol Security participates with area law enforcement 
agencies in apprehending alleged criminals and in joinl crime prevention 
programs, training classes, community service activities and memberships In 
mutual professional organizations.
How are crimes on campus reported and to whom?
It is Important that all crimes occurring on campus be immedialely reported to 
Campus Police lo ensure that appropriate action Is taken.
Crimes occurring on campus can be reported in person, or by calling Campus 
Police at 268-2323 any time of Ihe day or night
What happens when a student discovers a tlwft or other crime?
Reports ol tliell or other crimes are reported lo Campus Police lor Investigation. 
Resident assistants are key In reporting criminal activity in Ihe residence halls, and 
are required lo keep a log ol incidents occurring during their shills. When 
appropriate, stall Irorn Housing or Sludenl Affairs may be involved in answerlng.a 
call for assistance
Wluit about reporting Incidents outside ol tlw residence halls?
There are 34 police emergency phones located across Ihe campus. Without 
dialing. Hie caller is Immedialely in conlacl with Ihe Campus Police. The location 
ol Hie call is automatically lecordcd and response is immediale. Campus Police 
may also be reached by calling 268-2323, or simply 2323 on any campus phone.
Are lirearms permitted on campus?
No The university prohibits Ihe possession or use ol lirearms. as well as any oilier 
weapons in or near Ihe residence halls, or on university piopeily. Only sworn 
Campus Police personnel are authorized lo carry weapons while on duly. While oil 
duly, no member ol Hie department is permitted to possess a weapon on campus 
properly Police training includes daylight and nighllime qualification with lirearms 
training including Ihe legal, moral and practical aspecls of carrying a weapon.
F.rn the university consider criminal records in admission 
or employment?
Yes lor specific job classifications, such as securily personnel. The application for 
admission to Carnegie Mellon does not request inlormation concerning any 
previous criminal convicllons: consequently Ihe criminal records ol applicants loi 
admission lo the university are not reviewed by Ihe Office of Admission. The 
university recognizes ils responsibility to ensure the salely ol the campus 
community and therefore evaluates an enrolled student's status with Ihe university 
in Ihe event ol his or her criminal conviction in public court.
What is the university's disciplinary role il a student is convicted 
of a criminal offense?
The Universily Committee on Discipline may review Ihe case when a student has 
been convicted in public courts ol serious crimes. Special attention is given to 
circumstances which constitute a potential Ihieat against Ihe university's ability to 
lunction in whole or in part In such a review the commitlee will determine whether 
the students presence at the universily will endanger the universily communily.
For details on Ihe disciplinary review ol students, consult the Sludenl Handbook.
How is Ihe campus environment maintained lor safe lighting 
and walkways?
Securily personnel assess Ihe physical condition ol campus facilities  including 
landscaping, grounds keeping and outdoor lighting  on their regular patrols 
ol university properly All securily stall and members ol the campus communily 
can repoit deficient physical conditions lo Ihe universily's Physical Planl via 
Ihe campus-wide electronic mail system oi by calling Ihe Department ol Securily 
directly
Building Safely
How are university lacilities and programs accessible to students, 
employees and guests?
As a private university, Carnegie Mellon does have Ihe right lo limit access lo Its 
campus and lo conlrol activities on Ihe campus. But, in the spirit ot academic 
freedom and free expression of ideas, Ihe universily permits and encourages 
freedom of speech and assembly by all persons. This includes the distribution ot 
leaflets and pelilions, as well as demonstrations or protests involving speaking, 
discussion or the distribution ol information outside universily buildings.
What restrictions apply to such activities?
The only limils on these activities are Ihe rights of Ihe members ol the universily 
communily and Ihe maintenance ol Ihe normal functioning ol the university. No 
activities which harm individuals, damage or deface property, block access lo 
university buildings or disrupl classes will be permitted. Public events, such as 
lectures, plays and concerts, are, ol course, open lo Ihe communily on a ticket or 
tree admission basis.
What types of student housing are available?
Carnegie Mellon has a number ol traditional residence halls wilh common bath 
lacilities as well as a number of residence halls with private or semi-private baths.
A number ol single sex areas as well as some co-ed facilities are available for 
undergraduates. As a rule, areas may be co-ed or single sex as bathroom facilities 
permil. Also offered are a variety ol aparlmenl spaces both on-campus In 
university-owned buildings as well as oll-campus in buildings renled for 
undergraduate housing.
How are room requests handled?
The universitys housing system Is basically a seniority one: with seniors choosing 
first, followed by juniors and Ihen by sophomores. In March, upperclassmen may 
select their roommates and specific rooms in seniority order for the fall semester. 
The university traditionally assigns between 1,000 and 1,100 entering freshmen lo 
available spaces. The order In which Ireshmen pay their deposits to the Olflce ol 
Admission determines the order in which housing preference requests are honored. 
The university is normally able lo accommodate preferences for assignment to 
single sex areas, but assignment to co-ed areas is not always possible.
Can students change rooms during the semester?
Housing assignments are virtually Immutable at Ihe beginning ol Ihe fall semester, 
but once into Ihe academic year room change requests can be accommodated. The 
best lime lo make a room change Is at the end ol Ihe tall semester, when the 
university traditionally has well over 100 vacancies lo offer students who request 
room changes.
How are guests admitted or identified in the residence halls?
All universily buildings are locked and permil entrance only to people wilh keys or 
people accompanying residents who have their own keys. At the three buildings 
with Ironl desks, visitors are asked to present their Carnegie Mellon photo ID card. 
Other individuals are directed lo Ihe centrex telephone to call the student whom they 
are visiting lo meel them at the front desk.
How are the entrances of buildings secured?
Every outside door Is checked daily to ensure Ihe entrance is functioning properly. 
The universily has replaced Ihe fire alarm system in several ol our buildings, where 
Ihe plan is to use one door as a main entrance and exit and to have the side doors 
operate only as emergency exits. All ol our residence halls will soon be on a similar 
plan with only one entrance and exit. Side doors would operate only when a lire 
alarm is pulled or during a power outage or similar emergency.
What are the standard security features used in Ihe residence halls?
Rooms in the university's residence halls are secured by Ihe Best Locking System.
In mosl cases, these locks are boll locks which provide an optimum degree ol 
securily lor individual rooms. When residents report keys missing or lost, or fail lo 
return keys al the end of the academic year, Ihe university quickly changes Ihe lock 
and issues new keys lo Ihe residents. The universitys procedure assures that only 
the currenl residents ol a particular room have keys lo that room. All of the first floor 
dormitory screens are "security screens." constructed ol a heavy mesh in frames 
attached lo the window Irame itself.
Who is on-duty" al the residence halls?
The university relies on the strength ol ils competent resident assistant (RA) staff. 
There are four lull-time professional residence life administrators, called area 
coordinators, and 70 student resident assistants who live in the residence halls 
and have a variety ol responsibilities lor administering the halls.
How are student housing residents informed about security 
procedures and enforcement?
Via Student Attairs. the resident assistance stall is regularly informed, as is Ihe 
campus community, ot various health and safety concerns. All resident assistants 
receive an extensive week-long training session for preparation in aiding and 
advising students in all non-academic issues. Campus Police sanctioned personal 
safety practices are taught to Ihe RAs who then advise residents through bulletin 
boards, meetings and workshops as needed, including programs lo heighten 
student awareness ol personal concerns such as Ihe dangers of drug and alcohol 
abuse and Ihe problems ol suicide and acquaintance rape. Security information 
programs are presented by security personnel lo resident students at least once an 
academic year with special attention to those areas which may be experiencing 
unusual security problems, as well as ott-campus rental units in locations where 
students have to walk on public streets to travel lo and from campus.
Are there special security procedures during iow-occupancy periods 
such as holidays and vacation periods?
During Thanksgiving break and spring break special attention is given lo making 
sure lhal buildings slay locked and secure wilh extra security monitoring. During 
Ihe winter break (irorn mid-December to mid-January) all but one ol the residence 
facilities are locked and inaccessible by Ihe normal residents. Morewood Gardens 
Is offered as an alternative lor those students who cannot travel (approximately 30 
or 40 students). Morewood Gardens is monitored via its front desk on a 24-hour 
basis. The Campus Police naturally increase their patrols of Morewood Gardens 
area during the winter break's low occupancy period.
What Is the university's policy on the housing ol guests?
Generally, guests are allowed in residence hall rooms il all residents of Ihe room 
agree lo Ihe arrangement, Universily policy permits students to have guests stay in 
their room lor two days before obtaining permission Irom the Housing Oflice to 
allow lor a longer slay. Wilh lhal exception, we are not normally able lo provide 
housing lor guests ol students or nonsludents during Ihe academic year. Vacancies 
where Ihey exist are only ottered as permanent spaces to other undergraduates 
interested in living in university housing tor Ihe remainder of Ihe academic year.
The housing oflice can answer specific questions regarding Ihe availability of 
accommodations lor students and guests.
Safety Communications
How Is the campus community informed ot the security, safely 
procedures and crime prevention programs?
Campus media and publications specific to security and safely issues regularly 
carry news and information lor Ihe universily communily. Weekly media include Ihe 
student newspaper, The Tartan, and The 8-1/2x11 News. A brochure about Ihe 
Campus Police oilers details of shuttle and escorl services for sludenls. The Student 
Handbook is updated annually and provides details about policies and procedures 
The widely read campus computer bulletin board is also used as an Immediate 
means ol communication.
The Campus Watch Program
The Campus Watch Program is designed to increase the awareness ol Ihe entire 
community at Carnegie Mellon. The concept ol Campus Walch includes two 
simple aims:
1. The sharing ol crime information by Campus Police.
2. The involvement of the entire communily in reporting suspicious activity or 
actual crime commission.
Crime Alerts
Campus Police issues alerts to Ihe communily about recently committed crimes. 
These include crimes committed on Ihe campus as well as in the neighborhoods ol 
Ihe city surrounding the universily. These alerts are issued about crime that is a 
threat lo members of the campus communily. Crime Alerts give as much detail as 
possible.about the crime Itself, as well as any description ol suspects or vehicle. 
Names of victims are never included in the alerts. The alerts end wilh tips lo avoid 
becoming a victim.
Newsletters
The Department of Securily publishes a monthly newsletter, the 'Crime Watch. "The 
newsletter provides a summary of crime during the past month. II also advises Ihe 
campus about recent crime trends such as con arlists or harassing phone calls. 
Seasonal alerts will be presented lo help inform Ihe campus about expected crime. 
Specialized crime lips will be presented about topics such as how lo safely use the 
Automatic Banking Machines.
Crime Prevention Education
Through Ihe year, Ihe Securily Department's Crime Prevention Unit is available to 
present safety and securily seminars in residence halls, deparlmenl offices and any 
other setting bolh on and ofl campus. These seminars can be tailored to meel Ihe 
needs of the group. The topics range Irom personal safety, rape preveniion. 
residence securily, office securily, self-defense tactics, vehicle thell and other 
topics. These seminars can be arranged by calling Ihe Campus Police al exl, 2323.
Drugs and Alcohol
What is Carnegie Melton's policy on alcoholic beverages and drugs?
The university's faculty, administrators and stall recognize the responsibility 
and potential harm inherenl In Ihe use of alcoholic beverages. The universily is 
committed lo support the laws ol Ihe Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and 
reflects that support in its policies and procedures.
What is the Pennsylvania law concerning alcoholic beverages?
The Commonwealth law stales that a person who is less than 21 years ol age and 
who attempts lo purchase, purchases, consumes, possesses or knowingly and 
intentionally transports any alcohol, liquor or malt beverages within Ihe slate 
commits a summary olfense. Misrepresentation ol age to a licensed dealer or 
other persons who sell or furnish Intoxicaling liquors constitutes a third degree 
misdemeanor. Likewise, a person commits a third degree misdemeanor lor selling 
or providing alcoholic beverages to a known minor.
What is the policy lor alcoholic beverages on campus or al 
Carnegie Mellon events?
The universily follows the Commonwealth's law regarding intoxicating beverages 
Students are expected to conduct themselves both individually and collectively in a 
responsible manner. Abusive or excessive consumption ot alcohol resulting in 
interference with the rights ol other persons, personal injury or damage to property 
will result in severe disciplinary action.' Violations ol Ihe universily's policy can lead
lo a line Imposed by Ihe university and the possibility ol suspension and expulsion 
Planning Social Events wilh Alcohol: Things you Should Know is a brochure lhal 
outlines the universily policy on alcohol and includes a form outlining the 
responsibility involved with serving alcohol al an event. For more inlormation, 
refer lo the Sludenl Handbook or contact Sludenl Attairs.
What about drugs on campus?
Campus Police are instructed to turn over to the Narcotics Squad ol the Pittsburgh 
Police any significant quantity ol dangerous drugs discovered in Ihe course ol 
performing Iheir duty. The medically unsupervised use or distribution ol potentially 
harmful drugs such as marijuana, hallucinogens, amphetamines, barbituales and 
opiates is illegal and subject to very harsh penalties While the university does nol 
assume the responsibility of acting as an arm of the law, members ol the academic 
community have no immunity Irom Ihe enforcement ol the law. Distribution and use 
ot these drugs may threaten Ihe physical and menial health of Ihe user, as well as 
the welfare of other students and ihe academic community. The disciplinary policy 
of the university permits laklng action beyond, or separate Irom, any which may be 
taken by civil aulhorities. Also, the university cannot and does nol deny access lo ils 
property to law enforcement agents seeking to uphold the Federal and Pennsylvania 
Drug Laws. The Student Handbook further outlines Carnegie Mellon's drug policy.

Carnegie Mellon sheds some light on campus security
Theres no reason to be in the dark about campus security. A team of Carnegie Mellon police officers, security guards, and housing and student affairs staff members work to J<eep students, faculty, staff 
and visitors informed and safe on the campus and adjacent areas. These professionals are concerned with the safety and welfare of the campus community and are best able to answer questions about 
campus security.

Dnnlol Froy/Torton Contributing Editor
Surviving aftermath of rape, assault
By HE EDI HOOVER
Tartan Contributing Editor
Rape and sexual assault are serious traumas, 
difficult to recover from and frighteningly com
mon. National [undergraduate] figures, de
pending on the definition of sexual assault, 
range from 5-25 percent of women experiening 
some form of unwanted sexual contact in col
lege. We have approximately 1500 women un
dergraduates at CMU, so we anticipate some
where on the order of50-100 incidents per year 
where theres some form of unwanted sexual 
contact [among undergrads], says Michael 
Murphy, the dean of Student Affairs. And 
when you add into that graduate students, 
faculty, and staff, the number becomes higher. 
Carnegie Mellons policy, as stated in the 
Student Handbook, says it is a violation of 
Carnegie Mellons community standards to have 
sexual contact with any member of the commu
nity without the clear, freely chosen consent of 
those involved. Murphy emphasizes that 
sexual assault is any unwanted sexual contact 
 its not a question of severity.
Many believe the University wants to keep 
incidents of rape and sexual assault quiet, to 
avoid bad publicity for CMU. Murphy says this 
is absolutely untrue. I think [we have] an 
aggressive program [to deal with rape and
sexual assault], and its important for people to 
know that weve taken it seriously. Periodi
cally you run across some people who think, 
Boy, you must really have a problem at CMU. 
So be it. Anyone who would act in a manner 
that would protect the public image of the 
institution by not addressing the problem is 
totally reprehensible.
The aggressive program, he says, includes 
three critical components. The first is the defi
nition of sexual assault as any unwanted sexual 
contact. The second is making sure survivors of 
rape and sexual assault have multiple points of 
entry into the system; they can talk to a man or 
a woman, someone without a lot of authority in 
the University or someone with a lot of author
ity, a student or a staff or faculty member  
whom ever they are most comfortable with. 
The third critical component, which Murphy 
especially emphasizes, is the total control that 
individual has over the communication. He or 
she can come in, explain the situation, talk 
about it, and be told exactly what the alterna
tives are. If the person decides to do nothing, 
nothing will be done. Furthermore, the entire 
communication will be kept strictly confiden
tial, says Murphy, unless the survivor requests 
otherwise.
Many resources are available to rape and
Tartnr nrr 5CTRo Stpr k3

MANNES
COLLEGE OF MUSIC
Artistry & Community
At Mamies they go together. The skills, understanding and originality of 
artistry aw fostered by a superb faculty in a caring and supports 
community. That s why Mannes graduates succeed.

TECHNICAL SERVICES 
TRAINEE REPRESENTATIVE
This position is accountable for providing technical assistance in 
respect to product recommendation, customer complaints and 
inquiries. Incumbent will assist technical representatives and 
order entry representatives in their day to day responsibilities.
Applicants must exhibit excellent problem solving skills and 
interpersonal skills. Must be willing to become a member of a selfdirected team and be able to administer technical knowledge 
through written and oral communication.
Incumbent should be pursuing a degree in science. Should be able 
to use a PC and various software programs. Should be able to work 
at least 15 hours a week between the months of September and 
April and be able to work a full 40 hour week in the months of May, 
June, July, and August.
Send resume to:Marilyn A. Apostolou 
Manager, Human Resources 
PPG Industries, Inc.
One PPG Place 
Pittsburgh, PA 15272

Student Senate is looking for interested people to come 
and serve as representatives for the student body. If you 
would like to run for the honor of representing your college 
within the Student Senate, you must have a petition signed by 
25 students within your college.
The following positions will be up for election on April 6 and 7:
CFA 4 Seats (2 single semester)
CIT 5 Seats (2 single semester)
GSIA 2 Seats
Heinz 2 Seats (1 single semester)
H&SS 3 Seats
IM 1 Seat
MCS 2 Seats
Miscellaneous 1 Seat, single semester 
SCS 2 Seats (1 single semester)
All petitions are due at the Skibo Hall 
Information Desk by March 23
Funded in full by your Student Activities Fee.

very year, a lot o people make a 
huge mistake on their taxes.They 
don't take advantage of tax deferral and 
wind up sending Uncle Sam money they 
could be saving for retirement.
Fortunately, that's a mistake you can 
easily avoid with TIAA-CREF SRAs. 
SRAs not only ease your current taxbite, they offer a remarkably easy way 
to build retirement incomeespecially 
for the "extras that your regular pension 
and Social Security benefits may not 
cover. Because your contributions are 
made in before-tax dollars, you pay less 
taxes now. And since all earnings on 
your SRA are tax-deferred as well, the
money you don't send to Washington 
works even harder for you. Down the 
road, that can make a dramatic difference 
in your quality of life.
What else makes SRAs so special?
A range of allocation choicesfrom the 
guaranteed security of TIAA to the 
diversified investment accounts of 
CREF's variable annuityall backed 
by the nation's number one retirement 
system.
Why write off the chance for a more 
rewarding retirement? Call today and 
learn more about how TIAA-CREF 
SRAs can help you enjoy many 
happy returns.
Benefit now from tax deferral. Call our SRA hotline 1800-842-2733, ext. 8016.
75 years of ensuring the future 
for those who shape it!
UNFORTUNATELY THIS IS WHERE 
PEOPLE ARE PUTTING 
TOO MANY RETIREMENT DOLLARS.
Kevin Chen/Tartan Photographer

The Tartan  Carnegie Mellon  8 March 1993
CINEMA SCOpE
Thursday, March 11
La Dolce Vita
Directed by famed Italian filmmaker Federico 
Fellini, this lengthy, trend-setting film stars 
Marcello Mastroianni as a reporter for a Rome 
tabloid. Mastroiannis character finds that his 
life in shallow Rome society is completely worth
less, but cant seem to find any way to change it.
Much more entertaining and less ambiguous 
than other Fellini films, the story and screenplay 
were written by Fellini, Ennio Flajano, Tullio 
Brunelli, and Brunello Rondi.
Earned an Academy Award for Piero Gherardis 
costume design. Also stars Anita Ekberg, Anouk 
Aime, Yvonne Fumeaux, Magali Noel, Alain 
Cuny, and Annibale Ninchi.
At 6, 9 pm, and midnight.
Friday, March 12
The Bodyguard
Whitney Houston stars as Rachel Marron, a 
highly popular superstar turned actress (hmmm 
... big stretch, ay?) who hires a bodyguard named 
Frank Farmer (played by Kevin Costner) to pro
tect her from an obsessive and potentially dan
gerous fan.
Frank is a man who lives by meticulous calcu
lation, is resolved to never mix business with 
pleasure, and is well known for his talents as a 
professional bodyguard. Rachel is a woman whose 
reason for being is recklessness and seductive 
emotion.
Ahh, yes, these two try to hide their emotions 
behind a constant struggle for power, but in the 
end, their passion for one another just has to give 
in. Sounds like the basis for an exciting, actionpacked, love flick to me. Besides, its probably 
just worth it to see Whitney Houston try to act.
At 5:45, 8,10:15 pm, and 12:15 am.
Saturday, March 13
Forever Young
Mel Gibson plays a pilot whose love (played by 
Isabel Glasser) gets into a car accident and ends 
up in a coma. He becomes so heartbroken that he 
asks his scientist friend (played by George Wendt) 
to freeze him for a year.
Oh no, not another frozen guy story you say? 
Well wait, theres more!
Seems Mels friend forgets all about him and 
leaves him frozen for 53 years. Then a little boy 
(Elijah Wood) finds him, confused and thawing, 
and gets his mom (Jamie Lee Curtis) to help. 
Together, the three of them help track down the 
long lost love.
Ready for an exciting adventure with a frozen 
heartbroken pilot? Go spend the buck.
At 6, 8,10 pm, and midnight.
Sunday, March 14
Fiend Without a Face
This 1958 British film was directed by Aurthur 
Crabtree and stars Marshall Thompson, Kim 
Parker, Terence Kilburn, Michael Balfour, and 
Gil Winfield.
A mad scientist materializes his thoughts in 
the forms of invisible brain-shaped creatures 
with coiled tails that like to eat people for their 
food.
The monsters are somewhat reminiscent of the 
Id creature from Forbidden Planet.
Features lots of great special effects and and a 
wonderfully horrific climax.
By Tina L. Urso
Beehive 
Forbes Ave.

U. SWEEKNDPC. IAL!.H&A R eHPW& allstWR  Music TWPFEHP
Pittsburgh Symphony Principal Trumpet George Vosburgh tells why 
he and the trumpet are the perfect match:
1 think certain personalities are drawn to certain instruments. 
So you can imagine that an introvert doesnt make 
for the best trumpet player. I think people are 
successful musicians when theres a good 
blend between their personality and the 
instrument theyve chosen.
Hear that harmonious blend 
this weekend 
when the 
Pittsburgh 
Symphony 
performs a thrilling 
program featuring 
Berlioz' exciting 
Symphonic 
fantastique.
Friday, March 12, 8:00 p.m. Saturday, March 13, 8:00 p.m. 
Sunday, March 14, 2:30 p.m.

in the Life olan Artist, Op. 14
